It calls `generateBuilder()` which extracts the schema for a specific CRD version, converts it to a Structural schema using `NewStructural()`, and then builds a complete OpenAPI v3 specification by converting the Structural schema to `spec.Schema` via `ToKubeOpenAPI()`. The builder then uses kube-openapi's `builder3.BuildOpenAPISpecFromRoutes()` to generate the final `spec3.OpenAPI` structure.\\n\\n5. **OpenAPI V3 Controller** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/controller/openapiv3/controller.go): The `Controller` watches CustomResourceDefinitions for changes. When a CRD is created or updated, it calls `buildV3Spec()` which invokes `builder.BuildOpenAPIV3()` to generate the OpenAPI v3 spec for that CRD's version. The controller then calls `updateCRDSpec()` and `updateGroupVersion()` to merge multiple CRD specs per group version and publish them to the OpenAPIV3Service.\\n\\n6. **OpenAPI Spec Publication - Registration** (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/routes/openapi.go): The `OpenAPI.InstallV3()` method registers the `/openapi/v3` HTTP endpoint by calling `openAPIVersionedService.RegisterOpenAPIV3VersionedService(\\\"/openapi/v3\\\", mux)`. This makes the endpoint accessible via the API server's HTTP mux.\\n\\n7. **OpenAPI Spec Endpoint Handler** (vendor/k8s.io/kube-openapi/pkg/handler3/handler.go): The `OpenAPIService` is responsible for serving the OpenAPI v3 specs at `/openapi/v3`. The `RegisterOpenAPIV3VersionedService()` method registers the HTTP handler, and requests to `/openapi/v3` and `/openapi/v3/{group-version}` are handled by the `HandleDiscovery` and group version methods, which return the cached OpenAPI specifications in JSON format.\\n\\nThis chain enables dynamic generation and publication of OpenAPI v3 schemas for custom resources, allowing API consumers to discover the schema of any CRD through the standard Kubernetes OpenAPI endpoint.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
